<li>1633–38 – <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Perfilyev" title="Ilya Perfilyev">Ilya Perfilyev</a> and Ivan Rebrov sail from Zhigansk in kochi some 800 kilometres (500 mi) downriver to the mouth of the Lena and sail along the coast east and west, reaching the mouths of the <a href="/wiki/Olenyok_River" title="Olenyok River">Olenyok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yana_River" title="Yana River">Yana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indigirka_River" title="Indigirka River">Indigirka</a> rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1638–40 – Poznik Ivanov crosses the <a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk_Range" title="Verkhoyansk Range">Verkhoyansk Range</a> into the upper reaches of the Yana, and then portages over the <a href="/wiki/Chersky_Range" title="Chersky Range">Chersky Range</a> into the Indigirka River system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1639–40 – <a href="/wiki/Maksim_Perfilyev" title="Maksim Perfilyev">Maksim Perfilyev</a> ascends the <a href="/wiki/Vitim_River" title="Vitim River">Vitim River</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tsipa_River" title="Tsipa River">Tsipa</a>, which he also ascends (until rapids force him to turn back), becoming the first Russian to enter <a href="/wiki/Transbaikal" title="Transbaikal">Transbaikal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1639–41 – <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Moskvitin" title="Ivan Moskvitin">Ivan Moskvitin</a> ascends the <a href="/wiki/Maya_River" title="Maya River">Maya</a>, portages across the <a href="/wiki/Dzhugdzhur_Mountains" title="Dzhugdzhur Mountains">Dzhugdzhur Mountains</a>, and descends the <a href="/wiki/Ulya_River" title="Ulya River">Ulya</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a>; two groups are sent to the north and south, reaching the mouths of the <a href="/wiki/Taui_Bay" title="Taui Bay">Taui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uda_River_(Khabarovsk_Krai)" title="Uda River (Khabarovsk Krai)">Uda</a> rivers, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-8"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1641 – Dmitri Zyrian discovers the <a href="/wiki/Alazeya_River" title="Alazeya River">Alazeya</a>, which he ascends as far as the <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-9"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1642–43 – <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> discovers "Anthony van Diemenslandt" (<a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>) and "Staten Landt" (<a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>); following year discovers "'t Eylandt Amsterdam" (<a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a>), <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">New Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quanchi_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-Quanchi-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1643 – <a href="/wiki/Kurbat_Ivanov" title="Kurbat Ivanov">Kurbat Ivanov</a> reaches the western shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>, opposite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olkhon" title="Olkhon">Olkhon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haywood_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haywood-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>1643 – <a href="/wiki/Maarten_Gerritsz_Vries" title="Maarten Gerritsz Vries">Maarten Gerritsz Vries</a> sails along the eastern coast of "Yezo" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokkaid%C5%8D" title="Hokkaidō">Hokkaidō</a>), between <a href="/wiki/Iturup" title="Iturup">Iturup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urup" title="Urup">Urup</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitfield_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-Whitfield-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li>1643 – Vasiliy Sychev discovers the <a href="/wiki/Anabar_River" title="Anabar River">Anabar</a>, where he establishes the <i>zimovie</i> Anabarskoye.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Armstrong2010_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Armstrong2010-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holland_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holland-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>1643–45 – <a href="/wiki/Vassili_Poyarkov" title="Vassili Poyarkov">Vassili Poyarkov</a> crosses the <a href="/wiki/Stanovoy_Range" title="Stanovoy Range">Stanovoy Range</a> and descends the <a href="/wiki/Zeya_River" title="Zeya River">Zeya</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur</a>, which he follows to its mouth; from here, he coasts along the Sea of Okhotsk to the Ulya (on the way sighting the <a href="/wiki/Shantar_Islands" title="Shantar Islands">Shantar Islands</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golder_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golder-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>1644 – Tasman maps the northern coast of Australia, connecting "Nova Guinea" (the Cape York Peninsula) with "the land of D'Eendracht" (Western Australia).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-5"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1644 – <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Stadukhin" title="Mikhail Stadukhin">Mikhail Stadukhin</a> reaches the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-10"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1644–47 – Ivan Pokhabov is the first to ascend the Angara to Lake Baikal, which he crosses to the <a href="/wiki/Selenga_River" title="Selenga River">Selenga</a>; he later ascends it and reaches <a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" title="Ulaanbaatar">Urga</a> (in present-day <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-11"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forsyth_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forsyth-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>1646 – Isaya Ignatyev reaches <a href="/wiki/Chaunskaya_Bay" title="Chaunskaya Bay">Chaunskaya Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vaughan_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vaughan-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>1648–49 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a> sails from the Kolyma, rounds <a href="/wiki/Cape_Dezhnev" title="Cape Dezhnev">Cape Dezhnev</a> (thus proving Asia and America are separate), and reaches the <a href="/wiki/Anadyr_River" title="Anadyr River">Anadyr River</a>, which he ascends for some 563 kilometres (350 mi) (here he builds the <i>zimovie</i> <a href="/wiki/Anadyrsk" title="Anadyrsk">Anadyrsk</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1649–51 – <a href="/wiki/Yerofey_Khabarov" title="Yerofey Khabarov">Yerofey Khabarov</a> ascends the <a href="/wiki/Olyokma_River" title="Olyokma River">Olyokma River</a>, crosses the northern <a href="/wiki/Yablonoi_Mountains" title="Yablonoi Mountains">Yablonoi Mountains</a>, and descends the Amur to its confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Songhua_River" title="Songhua River">Songhua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golder_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Golder-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>1650 – Stadukhin and Semen Motora travel from the Kolyma, across the Anyuyskiy Range, to Anadyrsk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1651–57 – Stadukhin travels from Anadyrsk to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Penzhina_Bay" title="Penzhina Bay">Penzhina River</a>, then west along the northern coast of the Sea of Okhotsk to <a href="/wiki/Okhotsk" title="Okhotsk">Okhotsk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-12"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1653–54 – Beketov ascends the <a href="/wiki/Khilok_River" title="Khilok River">Khilok</a>, crosses the southern Yablonoi Mountains, and descends the <a href="/wiki/Ingoda_River" title="Ingoda River">Ingoda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shilka_River" title="Shilka River">Shilka</a> rivers to the latter's confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Nercha_River" title="Nercha River">Nercha</a> (where his men build the ostrog <a href="/wiki/Nerchinsk" title="Nerchinsk">Nerchinsk</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-13"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1654 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9dard_Chouart_des_Groseilliers" title="Médard Chouart des Groseilliers">Médard Chouart des Groseilliers</a> explores the entire western shore of Lake Michigan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeVoto_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeVoto-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>1659 – Groseilliers and <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Esprit_Radisson" title="Pierre-Esprit Radisson">Pierre-Esprit Radisson</a> explore the southern shore of Lake Superior as far west as <a href="/wiki/Chequamegon_Bay" title="Chequamegon Bay">Chequamegon Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeVoto_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeVoto-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>1661 – <a href="/wiki/Johann_Grueber" title="Johann Grueber">Johann Grueber</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albert_Dorville" title="Albert Dorville">Albert Dorville</a> are the first to visit <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sandberg_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sandberg-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li>1669 – <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9-Robert_Cavelier,_Sieur_de_La_Salle" title="René-Robert Cavelier, Sieur de La Salle">Robert de la Salle</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio</a>, descending it as far as the <a href="/wiki/Falls_of_the_Ohio_National_Wildlife_Conservation_Area" title="Falls of the Ohio National Wildlife Conservation Area">Falls of Ohio</a> at the site of modern <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkman_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parkman-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li>1673 – <a href="/wiki/Louis_Jolliet" title="Louis Jolliet">Louis Jolliet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Marquette" title="Jacques Marquette">Jacques Marquette</a> reach the upper Mississippi, descending it to its confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas</a>; also discover the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkman_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Parkman-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li>1675 – <a href="/wiki/Anthony_de_la_Roch%C3%A9" title="Anthony de la Roché">Anthony de la Roché</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_Island" title="South Georgia Island">South Georgia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>1682 – Robert de La Salle descends the "Rivière de Colbert" (<a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>) to its mouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkman_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-Parkman-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li>1688–89 – <a href="/wiki/Jacques_de_Noyon" title="Jacques de Noyon">Jacques de Noyon</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Rainy_Lake" title="Rainy Lake">Rainy Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_of_the_Woods" title="Lake of the Woods">Lake of the Woods</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeVoto_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-DeVoto-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>1690–92 – <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kelsey" title="Henry Kelsey">Henry Kelsey</a> travels from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/York_Factory,_Manitoba" title="York Factory, Manitoba">York Factory</a> southwestward, probably reaching the <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan_River" title="Saskatchewan River">Saskatchewan</a> and the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Assiniboine_River" title="Assiniboine River">Assiniboine</a>—in the process becoming the first European to see the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Prairies" title="Canadian Prairies">Canadian Prairies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeVoto_71-3"><a href="#cite_note-DeVoto-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>1696 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luka_Morozko" title="Luka Morozko">Luka Morozko</a> travels almost halfway down the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka</a>, reaching the <a href="/wiki/Tigil_River" title="Tigil River">Tigil River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1697–99 – <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Atlasov" title="Vladimir Atlasov">Vladimir Atlasov</a> reaches as far as the <a href="/wiki/Golygina_River" title="Golygina River">Golygina River</a> on the southwest coast of Kamchatka, from which he sights <a href="/wiki/Atlasov_Island" title="Atlasov Island">Atlasov Island</a>; also crosses the <a href="/wiki/Sredinny_Range" title="Sredinny Range">Sredinny Range</a> (twice), reaching <a href="/wiki/Olyutorsky_Gulf" title="Olyutorsky Gulf">Olyutorsky Gulf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_River" title="Kamchatka River">Kamchatka River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantzeff_46-14"><a href="#cite_note-Lantzeff-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-4"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_European_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cook_new_zealand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="499" decoding="async" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Cook_new_zealand.jpg/220px-Cook_new_zealand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Cook_new_zealand.jpg/330px-Cook_new_zealand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Cook_new_zealand.jpg/440px-Cook_new_zealand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cook_new_zealand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cook's map of New Zealand</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hodges,_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1770" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg/220px-Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg/330px-Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg/440px-Hodges%2C_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hodges,_Resolution_and_Adventure_in_Matavai_Bay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HMS_Resolution_(Cook)" title="HMS Resolution (Cook)">Resolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Adventure_(1771)" title="HMS Adventure (1771)">Adventure</a> in Matavai Bay</i> by <a href="/wiki/William_Hodges" title="William Hodges">William Hodges</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver-Rainier.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Vancouver-Rainier.jpg/220px-Vancouver-Rainier.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Vancouver-Rainier.jpg/330px-Vancouver-Rainier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Vancouver-Rainier.jpg/440px-Vancouver-Rainier.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver-Rainier.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Mount Rainier from the south Part of Admiralty Inlet". The mountain was discovered by Vancouver during his exploration of Puget Sound in the spring of 1792.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg/300px-Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg/450px-Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alex_MacKenzie_from_Canada_by_land.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inscription at the end of the Alexander Mackenzie's Canada crossing located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Timeline_of_European_exploration&amp;params=52_22_43_N_127_28_14_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">52°22′43″N</span> <span class="longitude">127°28′14″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">52.37861°N 127.47056°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">52.37861; -127.47056</span></span></span></a></span></div></div></div>
<ul><li>1706 – Mikhail Nasedkin reaches <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lopatka" title="Cape Lopatka">Cape Lopatka</a> and sights <a href="/wiki/Shumshu" title="Shumshu">Shumshu</a>, northernmost of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-5"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1710 – <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Permyakov" title="Yakov Permyakov">Yakov Permyakov</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Bolshoy_Lyakhovsky_Island" title="Bolshoy Lyakhovsky Island">Bolshoy Lyakhovsky Island</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>1713 – Ivan Kozyrevsky reaches Shumshu and <a href="/wiki/Paramushir" title="Paramushir">Paramushir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_67-6"><a href="#cite_note-March-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>1714 – <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_de_Veniard,_Sieur_de_Bourgmont" title="Étienne de Veniard, Sieur de Bourgmont">Étienne de Veniard, Sieur de Bourgmont</a> ascends the Missouri as far as the <a href="/wiki/Platte_River" title="Platte River">Platte</a>, becoming the first to enter the present-day <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1720 – Pedro de Villasur travels from Santa Fe, through what is now part of southeastern <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, to the lower Platte in eastern Nebraska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1722 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakob_Roggeveen" title="Jakob Roggeveen">Jakob Roggeveen</a> discovers "Paasch Eiland" (<a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Tutuila" title="Tutuila">Tutuila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fischer2005_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer2005-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tcherkezoff_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tcherkezoff-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li>1728 – <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a> sails through the strait that now bears his name; also discovers and names <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Island" title="Saint Lawrence Island">Saint Lawrence Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vaughan_43-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vaughan-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>1732 – <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gvozdev" title="Mikhail Gvozdev">Mikhail Gvozdev</a> discovers the "Large Country" (<a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golder_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-Golder-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>1734 – <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_de_La_V%C3%A9rendrye" title="Jean Baptiste de La Vérendrye">Jean Baptiste de La Vérendrye</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipeg" title="Lake Winnipeg">Lake Winnipeg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeVoto_71-4"><a href="#cite_note-DeVoto-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>1734–37 – Stepan Muravev and Mikhail Pavlov chart the Russian coast from <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a> to just east of the <a href="/wiki/Pechora_River" title="Pechora River">Pechora</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Malygin" title="Stepan Malygin">Stepan Malygin</a> charts it from there to the Ob River, including the <a href="/wiki/Yamal_Peninsula" title="Yamal Peninsula">Yamal Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1735–36 – <a href="/wiki/Vasili_Pronchishchev" title="Vasili Pronchishchev">Vasili Pronchishchev</a> charts the Russian coast from the Lena west to the <a href="/wiki/Khatanga_River" title="Khatanga River">Khatanga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1737 – <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Ovtsyn" title="Dmitry Ovtsyn">Dmitry Ovtsyn</a> charts the Russian coast from the mouth of the Ob to the Yenisei.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1738 – <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gaultier_de_Varennes,_sieur_de_La_V%C3%A9rendrye" title="Pierre Gaultier de Varennes, sieur de La Vérendrye">Pierre de La Vérendrye</a> visits <a href="/wiki/Mandan" title="Mandan">Mandan</a> villages near the site of present-day <a href="/wiki/Bismarck,_North_Dakota" title="Bismarck, North Dakota">Bismarck, North Dakota</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkman1893_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parkman1893-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li>1738–40 – <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Minin" title="Fyodor Minin">Fyodor Minin</a> charts the Russian coast from the Yenisei to the Pyasina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-8"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1739 – <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Charles_Bouvet_de_Lozier" title="Jean-Baptiste Charles Bouvet de Lozier">Jean Bouvet de Lozier</a> discovers "Cape Circumcision" (<a href="/wiki/Bouvet_Island" title="Bouvet Island">Bouvet Island</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1739–41 – <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Laptev" title="Dmitry Laptev">Dmitry Laptev</a> charts the Russian coast from the Lena to just east of the Kolyma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-9"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1741 – Bering sights <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Elias" title="Mount Saint Elias">Mount St. Elias</a>, the entrance of <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a> (from Cape Providence to Chignik Bay) and several of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> (discovering <a href="/wiki/Great_Sitkin_Island" title="Great Sitkin Island">Great Sitkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atka_Island" title="Atka Island">Atka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kiska" title="Kiska">Kiska</a>), as well as discovering <a href="/wiki/Kayak_Island" title="Kayak Island">Kayak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montague_Island_(Alaska)" title="Montague Island (Alaska)">Montague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinchinbrook_Island_(Alaska)" title="Hinchinbrook Island (Alaska)">Hinchinbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sitkalidak_Island" title="Sitkalidak Island">Sitkalidak</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Shumagin_Islands" title="Shumagin Islands">Shumagin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a>; his second-in-command, <a href="/wiki/Aleksei_Chirikov" title="Aleksei Chirikov">Aleksei Chirikov</a>, sights <a href="/wiki/Mount_Fairweather" title="Mount Fairweather">Mounts Fairweather</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Douglas_(Alaska)" title="Mount Douglas (Alaska)">Douglas</a> and discovers Noyes and <a href="/wiki/Baker_Island_(Alaska)" title="Baker Island (Alaska)">Baker Islands</a> (both off the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Island_(Alaska)" title="Prince of Wales Island (Alaska)">Prince of Wales Island</a>), as well as <a href="/wiki/Baranof_Island" title="Baranof Island">Baranof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chichagof_Island" title="Chichagof Island">Chichagof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kruzof_Island" title="Kruzof Island">Kruzof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yakobi_Island" title="Yakobi Island">Yakobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afognak" title="Afognak">Afognak</a>, the Aleutian Islands (<a href="/wiki/Umnak" title="Umnak">Umnak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adak_Island" title="Adak Island">Adak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agattu" title="Agattu">Agattu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attu_Island" title="Attu Island">Attu</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Islands_of_Four_Mountains" title="Islands of Four Mountains">Islands of Four Mountains</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Kenai_Peninsula" title="Kenai Peninsula">Kenai Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golder1922_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golder1922-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>1741–42 – <a href="/wiki/Khariton_Laptev" title="Khariton Laptev">Khariton Laptev</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semion_Chelyuskin" title="Semion Chelyuskin">Semion Chelyuskin</a> chart the <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a>, with the latter reaching <a href="/wiki/Cape_Chelyuskin" title="Cape Chelyuskin">Cape Chelyuskin</a>, the northernmost point of Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lincoln_45-10"><a href="#cite_note-Lincoln-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1742 – <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Middleton_(navigator)" title="Christopher Middleton (navigator)">Christopher Middleton</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Wager_Bay" title="Wager Bay">Wager Bay</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Repulse_Bay,_Nunavut" title="Repulse Bay, Nunavut">Repulse Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2003_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams2003-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>1742–43 – <a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_Gaultier_de_La_V%C3%A9rendrye" title="Louis-Joseph Gaultier de La Vérendrye">Louis-Joseph Gaultier de La Vérendrye</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_La_V%C3%A9rendrye" title="François de La Vérendrye">François</a> reach the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Horn_Mountains" title="Big Horn Mountains">Big Horn Mountains</a> of modern <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>; on their return they reach the vicinity of present-day <a href="/wiki/Pierre,_South_Dakota" title="Pierre, South Dakota">Pierre, South Dakota</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkman1893_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Parkman1893-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>1747 – Jeremiah Westall discovers <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_Inlet" title="Chesterfield Inlet">Chesterfield Inlet</a> and sails about sixty miles up it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2003_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Williams2003-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>1761–62 – William Christopher sails 370 kilometres (230 mi) into Chesterfield Inlet to the western end of <a href="/wiki/Baker_Lake,_Nunavut" title="Baker Lake, Nunavut">Baker Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2003_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Williams2003-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>1767 – <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wallis" title="Samuel Wallis">Samuel Wallis</a> discovers "King George's Land" (<a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>1769 – José Ortega discovers <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes2007_39-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes2007-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>1769–70 – <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> circumnavigates both islands of New Zealand, proving they aren't part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terra_Australis_Incognita" title="Terra Australis Incognita">Terra Australis Incognita</a>; also discovers the east coast of Australia from <a href="/wiki/Cape_Howe" title="Cape Howe">Cape Howe</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_York_Peninsula" title="Cape York Peninsula">Cape York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>1771–72 – <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Hearne" title="Samuel Hearne">Samuel Hearne</a> reaches the <a href="/wiki/Coppermine_River" title="Coppermine River">Coppermine</a>, descending it to what would become known as <a href="/wiki/Coronation_Gulf" title="Coronation Gulf">Coronation Gulf</a>; the following year, on his way back, he becomes the first to sight and cross <a href="/wiki/Great_Slave_Lake" title="Great Slave Lake">Great Slave Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-6"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1772 – <a href="/wiki/Yves-Joseph_de_Kerguelen-Tr%C3%A9marec" title="Yves-Joseph de Kerguelen-Trémarec">Yves-Joseph de Kerguelen-Trémarec</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Kerguelen_Islands" title="Kerguelen Islands">Kerguelen Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1772 – <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fages" title="Pedro Fages">Pedro Fages</a> sights the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li>1773 – <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Lyakhov" title="Ivan Lyakhov">Ivan Lyakhov</a> reaches <a href="/wiki/Kotelny_Island" title="Kotelny Island">Kotelny Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vaughan_43-5"><a href="#cite_note-Vaughan-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>1773–75 – Cook is the first to cross the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Circle" title="Antarctic Circle">Antarctic Circle</a>, reaching 71° 10’ S, thus finally disproving the existence of Terra Australis Incognita; also discovers <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Sandwich Islands">South Sandwich Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>1774 – <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_P%C3%A9rez_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Juan José Pérez Hernández">Juan José Pérez Hernández</a> explores the western coast of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cape_Mendocino" title="Cape Mendocino">Cape Mendocino</a> northwards, discovering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Charlotte_Islands" title="Queen Charlotte Islands">Queen Charlotte Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dall_Island" title="Dall Island">Dall Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes2001_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes2001-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li>1775 – <a href="/wiki/Bruno_de_Heceta" title="Bruno de Heceta">Bruno de Heceta</a> discovers the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_River" title="Columbia River">Columbia River</a>; his consort <a href="/wiki/Juan_Francisco_de_la_Bodega_y_Quadra" title="Juan Francisco de la Bodega y Quadra">Juan Francisco de la Bodega y Quadra</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Island_(Alaska)" title="Prince of Wales Island (Alaska)">Prince of Wales Island</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bucareli_Bay" title="Bucareli Bay">Bucareli Bay</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes1999_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes1999-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>1776 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Atanasio_Dom%C3%ADnguez" title="Francisco Atanasio Domínguez">Francisco Atanasio Domínguez</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silvestre_V%C3%A9lez_de_Escalante" title="Silvestre Vélez de Escalante">Silvestre Vélez de Escalante</a> follow the Rio Grande north to the modern state of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, where they travel west, discovering <a href="/wiki/Utah_Lake" title="Utah Lake">Utah Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-7"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1777–78 – Cook discovers <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Christmas Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>; also explores the Alaskan coast as far north as <a href="/wiki/Icy_Cape,_Alaska" title="Icy Cape, Alaska">Icy Cape</a>, discovering <a href="/wiki/Cook_Inlet" title="Cook Inlet">Cook Inlet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>1787 – <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Barkley" title="Charles William Barkley">Charles William Barkley</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Juan_de_Fuca" title="Strait of Juan de Fuca">Strait of Juan de Fuca</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2003_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-Williams2003-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>1788 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_Arthur_Phillip" title="Captain Arthur Phillip">Captain Arthur Phillip</a> arrives with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_First_Fleet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The First Fleet (page does not exist)">The First Fleet</a> in <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a> on the coast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sydney,_Australia" title="Sydney, Australia">Sydney, Australia</a>.</li>
<li>1789 – <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Mackenzie_(explorer)" title="Alexander Mackenzie (explorer)">Alexander Mackenzie</a> descends the <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_River" title="Mackenzie River">Mackenzie River</a> to its mouth in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mackenzie1801_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mackenzie1801-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>1791 – <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Eliza" title="Francisco de Eliza">Francisco de Eliza</a> discovers the "Canal de Nuestra Señora del Rosario" (<a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Georgia" title="Strait of Georgia">Strait of Georgia</a>); <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Narv%C3%A1ez" title="José María Narváez">José María Narváez</a> explores up it, passing the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Fraser_River" title="Fraser River">Fraser River</a> and reaching as far north as <a href="/wiki/Texada_Island" title="Texada Island">Texada Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes1999_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes1999-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>1791–94 – <a href="/wiki/George_Vancouver" title="George Vancouver">George Vancouver</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/William_Robert_Broughton" title="William Robert Broughton">William Broughton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Puget" title="Peter Puget">Peter Puget</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Whidbey" title="Joseph Whidbey">Joseph Whidbey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Johnstone_(explorer)" title="James Johnstone (explorer)">James Johnstone</a>, charts the modern states of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" title="Washington (U.S. state)">Washington</a>, the coast of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Panhandle" title="Alaska Panhandle">Alaska Panhandle</a>, discovering <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Island" title="Admiralty Island">Admiralty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitkof_Island" title="Mitkof Island">Mitkof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrangell_Island" title="Wrangell Island">Wrangell Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago" title="Alexander Archipelago">Alexander Archipelago</a>, as well as proving the insularity of <a href="/wiki/Kuiu_Island" title="Kuiu Island">Kuiu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Revillagigedo_Island" title="Revillagigedo Island">Revillagigedo Islands</a>; also charts <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Inlet" title="Admiralty Inlet">Admiralty Inlet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puget_Sound" title="Puget Sound">Puget Sound</a> and discovers the <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Islands" title="Chatham Islands">Chatham Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snares_Islands_/_Tini_Heke" title="Snares Islands / Tini Heke">The Snares</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vancouver_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vancouver-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li>1792 – <a href="/wiki/Dionisio_Alcal%C3%A1_Galiano" title="Dionisio Alcalá Galiano">Dionisio Alcalá Galiano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cayetano_Vald%C3%A9s_y_Flores" title="Cayetano Valdés y Flores">Cayetano Valdés y Flores</a> circumnavigate Vancouver Island, proving its insularity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-8"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1792 – <a href="/wiki/Jacinto_Caama%C3%B1o" title="Jacinto Caamaño">Jacinto Caamaño</a> enters <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Strait" title="Clarence Strait">Clarence Strait</a>, showing that much of the Alaska Panhandle is an archipelago, not mainland, as had been presumed; also sights the southwest coast of Revillagigedo Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-9"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1792–93 – Mackenzie ascends the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_River_(Canada)" title="Peace River (Canada)">Peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parsnip_River" title="Parsnip River">Parsnip</a>, crosses the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Rockies" title="Canadian Rockies">Canadian Rockies</a> to the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Fraser_River" title="Fraser River">Fraser</a>, ascends the <a href="/wiki/West_Road_River" title="West Road River">West Road River</a> and crosses the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Mountains" title="Coast Mountains">Coast Mountains</a>, reaching the <a href="/wiki/Bella_Coola_River" title="Bella Coola River">Bella Coola</a>, which he descends to <a href="/wiki/North_Bentinck_Arm" title="North Bentinck Arm">North Bentinck Arm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dean_Channel" title="Dean Channel">Dean Channel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mackenzie1801_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mackenzie1801-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>1796 – <a href="/wiki/Mungo_Park_(explorer)" title="Mungo Park (explorer)">Mungo Park</a> reaches the upper <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a>, exploring it from <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9gou" title="Ségou">Ségou</a> to <a href="/wiki/Silla,_Mali" title="Silla, Mali">Silla</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li>1797–98 – <a href="/wiki/George_Bass" title="George Bass">George Bass</a> explores from Cape Howe to <a href="/wiki/Western_Port" title="Western Port">Western Port</a>, discovering <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">Bass Strait</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-6"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1798 – <a href="/wiki/John_Fearn_(whaler)" title="John Fearn (whaler)">John Fearn</a> discovers "Pleasant Island" (<a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quanchi_35-5"><a href="#cite_note-Quanchi-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>1798 – <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Lacerda" title="Francisco de Lacerda">Francisco de Lacerda</a> travels from <a href="/wiki/Tete,_Mozambique" title="Tete, Mozambique">Tete</a> northwest to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mweru" title="Lake Mweru">Lake Mweru</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1798–99 – <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Flinders" title="Matthew Flinders">Matthew Flinders</a> and George Bass circumnavigate Tasmania, proving its insularity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-7"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_European_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track,_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America,_published_1814.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3043" data-file-width="7000" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg/250px-Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg/375px-Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg/500px-Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track%2C_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America%2C_published_1814.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Lewis_and_Clark%27s_Track,_Across_the_Western_Portion_of_North_America,_published_1814.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The famous map of Lewis and Clark's expedition. It changed mapping of northwest America by providing the first accurate depiction of the relationship of the sources of the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_River" title="Columbia River">Columbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri</a> rivers, and the Rocky Mountains.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Descent_of_Fraser_River_1808.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="309" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Descent_of_Fraser_River_1808.jpg/220px-Descent_of_Fraser_River_1808.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/10/Descent_of_Fraser_River_1808.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Descent_of_Fraser_River_1808.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Colour drawing of Simon Fraser's 1808 descent of the Fraser River.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour,_Sept._26th,_1819.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="671" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg/220px-The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg/330px-The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg/440px-The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour%2C_Sept._26th%2C_1819.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Crews_of_H.M.S._Hecla_%26_Griper_Cutting_Into_Winter_Harbour,_Sept._26th,_1819.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The Crews of H.M.S. Hecla &amp; Griper Cutting Into Winter Harbour, Sept. 26th, 1819". An engraving from the journal published in 1821.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Point_Turnagain.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Point_Turnagain.jpg/220px-Point_Turnagain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Point_Turnagain.jpg/330px-Point_Turnagain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Point_Turnagain.jpg/440px-Point_Turnagain.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Point_Turnagain.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John Franklin's party encamped at Point Turnagain, the furthest point he reached.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg/220px-Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg/330px-Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg/440px-Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nlc_hms_investigator.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HMS <i>Investigator</i>, on the northwestern coast of Banks Island, 20 August 1851.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McClure_Map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/McClure_Map.jpg/250px-McClure_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/McClure_Map.jpg/375px-McClure_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/McClure_Map.jpg/500px-McClure_Map.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McClure_Map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map drawn by Robert McClure detailing the Northwest Passage, including the 1851 route of the <i>Investigator</i>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3617" data-file-width="2516" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg/170px-Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg/255px-Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg/340px-Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matterhorn_ascent_Dore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first ascent of the Matterhorn, by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Dor%C3%A9" title="Gustave Doré">Gustave Doré</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="1950" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg/250px-Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg/375px-Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg/500px-Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fly_River_Map_1876_NLA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original survey map created by L.M. D'Albertis in 1876.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg"><img alt="A group of men pose on the ice with dogs and sledges, with the ship's outline visible in the background" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="2044" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg/220px-Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg/330px-Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg/440px-Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nansen_Johansen_depart_14_March_1895.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nansen and Johansen finally depart on their polar journey, 14 March 1895. Nansen is the tall figure, second from left; Johansen is standing second from right.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>1800 – <a href="/wiki/James_Grant_(navigator)" title="James Grant (navigator)">James Grant</a> discovers the Australian coastline from <a href="/wiki/Cape_Banks" title="Cape Banks">Cape Banks</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Otway" title="Cape Otway">Cape Otway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-8"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>c. 1801–04 – A fur trading post is built on <a href="/wiki/Great_Bear_Lake" title="Great Bear Lake">Great Bear Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keith_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keith-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li>1802 – <a href="/wiki/John_Murray_(Australian_explorer)" title="John Murray (Australian explorer)">John Murray</a> discovers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Phillip_Bay" title="Port Phillip Bay">Port Phillip Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-9"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1802 – Matthew Flinders explores the coast from <a href="/wiki/Fowlers_Bay,_South_Australia" title="Fowlers Bay, South Australia">Fowlers Bay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Encounter_Bay" title="Encounter Bay">Encounter Bay</a>, discovering <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Gulf" title="Spencer Gulf">Spencer Gulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Island" title="Kangaroo Island">Kangaroo Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_St_Vincent" title="Gulf St Vincent">Gulf St. Vincent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-10"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1802 – <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Baudin" title="Nicolas Baudin">Nicolas Baudin</a> explores the coast from Cape Banks to Encounter Bay, where he meets Flinders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-11"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1802–03 – Flinders circumnavigates Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_62-12"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>1805–06 – <a href="/wiki/Meriwether_Lewis" title="Meriwether Lewis">Meriwether Lewis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Clark_(explorer)" title="William Clark (explorer)">William Clark</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mandan" title="Fort Mandan">Fort Mandan</a>, ascend the Missouri to its headwaters, cross the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_of_the_Americas" title="Continental Divide of the Americas">Continental Divide</a> via <a href="/wiki/Lemhi_Pass" title="Lemhi Pass">Lemhi Pass</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bitterroot_Range" title="Bitterroot Range">Bitterroot Range</a> to enter the present state of <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>, and descend the <a href="/wiki/Clearwater_River_(Idaho)" title="Clearwater River (Idaho)">Clearwater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snake_River" title="Snake River">Snake rivers</a> to the Columbia, which they descend to its mouth; on the way back Lewis explores the <a href="/wiki/Blackfoot_River_(Montana)" title="Blackfoot River (Montana)">Blackfoot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sun_River" title="Sun River">Sun rivers</a>, as well as the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Marias_River" title="Marias River">Marias</a>, while Clark travels through <a href="/wiki/Bozeman_Pass" title="Bozeman Pass">Bozeman Pass</a> and descends the <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_River" title="Yellowstone River">Yellowstone</a> to its confluence with the Missouri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ambrose_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ambrose-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li>1805–06 – Mungo Park descends the Niger as far as the Bussa rapids, where he is drowned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li>1806 – <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Sannikov" title="Yakov Sannikov">Yakov Sannikov</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/New_Siberia" title="New Siberia">New Siberia Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1806 – <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Bristow" title="Abraham Bristow">Abraham Bristow</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Islands" title="Auckland Islands">Auckland Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mawar_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mawar-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>1808 – <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fraser_(explorer)" title="Simon Fraser (explorer)">Simon Fraser</a> descends the <a href="/wiki/Fraser_River" title="Fraser River">Fraser River</a> for some 800 kilometres (500 mi) to its mouth, reaching the Strait of Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-10"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1810 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Hasselborough" title="Frederick Hasselborough">Frederick Hasselborough</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Campbell_Island,_New_Zealand" title="Campbell Island, New Zealand">Campbell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Island" title="Macquarie Island">Macquarie Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-3"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1811–12 – <a href="/wiki/W._Price_Hunt" title="W. Price Hunt">Wilson Price Hunt</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Union_Pass" title="Union Pass">Union Pass</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Range" title="Wind River Range">Wind River Range</a> and reaches the upper Snake River, while <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stuart_(explorer)" title="Robert Stuart (explorer)">Robert Stuart</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/South_Pass_(Wyoming)" title="South Pass (Wyoming)">South Pass</a>—his route would later become the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Trail" title="Oregon Trail">Oregon Trail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-11"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1816 – <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Kotzebue" title="Otto von Kotzebue">Otto von Kotzebue</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue_Sound" title="Kotzebue Sound">Kotzebue Sound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-12"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1819 – <a href="/wiki/William_Smith_(mariner)" title="William Smith (mariner)">William Smith</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetland_Islands" title="South Shetland Islands">South Shetland Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riffenburgh_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Riffenburgh-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li>1819–20 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Edward_Parry" title="William Edward Parry">William Edward Parry</a> enters <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_Sound" title="Lancaster Sound">Lancaster Sound</a> and reaches <a href="/wiki/Melville_Island_(Northwest_Territories_and_Nunavut)" title="Melville Island (Northwest Territories and Nunavut)">Melville Island</a>, discovering and naming <a href="/wiki/Cornwallis_Island_(Nunavut)" title="Cornwallis Island (Nunavut)">Cornwallis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bathurst_Island_(Canada)" title="Bathurst Island (Canada)">Bathurst</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Island_(Nunavut)" title="Somerset Island (Nunavut)">Somerset Islands</a>; the following year sights "Banks Land" (<a href="/wiki/Banks_Island" title="Banks Island">Banks Island</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parry_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parry-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li>1820 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Bransfield" title="Edward Bransfield">Edward Bransfield</a> sights the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Peninsula" title="Antarctic Peninsula">Antarctic Peninsula</a>; also discovers northernmost islands of the South Shetlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-4"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1820–21 – <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen</a> discovers the northernmost islands of the South Sandwich group; following year discovers <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_Island" title="Peter I Island">Peter I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Island" title="Alexander Island">Alexander Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li>1821 – <a href="/wiki/John_Franklin" title="John Franklin">John Franklin</a> explores over 800 kilometres (500 mi) of coastline from the mouth of the Coppermine River to Point Turnagain on the <a href="/wiki/Kent_Peninsula" title="Kent Peninsula">Kent Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franklin_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Franklin-95">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li>1821 – Sealers <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Palmer" title="Nathaniel Palmer">Nathaniel Palmer</a> and George Powell discover "Powell's Islands" (<a href="/wiki/South_Orkney_Islands" title="South Orkney Islands">South Orkney Islands</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spears_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spears-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li>1821–23 – Parry explores the eastern side of the <a href="/wiki/Melville_Peninsula" title="Melville Peninsula">Melville Peninsula</a>, reaching the western entrance of <a href="/wiki/Fury_and_Hecla_Strait" title="Fury and Hecla Strait">Fury and Hecla Strait</a>; also explores the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Foxe_Basin" title="Foxe Basin">Foxe Basin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parry1824_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parry1824-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>1823 – <a href="/wiki/Dixon_Denham" title="Dixon Denham">Dixon Denham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Oudney" title="Walter Oudney">Walter Oudney</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Clapperton" title="Hugh Clapperton">Hugh Clapperton</a> are the first Europeans to sight <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li>1823 – Sealer <a href="/wiki/James_Weddell" title="James Weddell">James Weddell</a> sails to 74°15′ S into "King George IV's Sea" (<a href="/wiki/Weddell_Sea" title="Weddell Sea">Weddell Sea</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weddell_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weddell-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li>1824 – <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Black" title="Samuel Black">Samuel Black</a> ascends the <a href="/wiki/Finlay_River" title="Finlay River">Finlay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Thutade_Lake" title="Thutade Lake">Thutade Lake</a>, source of the Finlay-Peace-Slave-Mackenzie river system; then portages to the <a href="/wiki/Stikine_River" title="Stikine River">Stikine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turnagain_River" title="Turnagain River">Turnagain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes2002_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes2002-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li>1824–25 – <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Provost" title="Étienne Provost">Étienne Provost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bridger" title="Jim Bridger">Jim Bridger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Skene_Ogden" title="Peter Skene Ogden">Peter Skene Ogden</a> independently reach <a href="/wiki/Great_Salt_Lake" title="Great Salt Lake">Great Salt Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-13"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1825–26 – Franklin explores the Arctic coastline from the mouth of the Mackenzie River west to Point Beechey, while his partner <a href="/wiki/John_Richardson_(naturalist)" title="John Richardson (naturalist)">John Richardson</a> explores east to the Coppermine River, naming <a href="/wiki/Dolphin_and_Union_Strait" title="Dolphin and Union Strait">Dolphin and Union Strait</a> and discovering "<a href="/wiki/Wollaston_Peninsula" title="Wollaston Peninsula">Wollaston Land</a>" (part of the southern coast of <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Island_(Canada)" title="Victoria Island (Canada)">Victoria Island</a>) — combining to chart over 1,930 kilometres (1,200 mi) of coastline; Richardson also surveys the five arms of Great Bear Lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franklin1828_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Franklin1828-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li>1826 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_Beechey" title="Frederick William Beechey">Frederick William Beechey</a> charts the Alaskan coastline from Icy Cape to <a href="/wiki/Point_Barrow" title="Point Barrow">Point Barrow</a>; also discovers <a href="/wiki/Vanavana" title="Vanavana">Vanavana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fangataufa" title="Fangataufa">Fangataufa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ahunui" title="Ahunui">Ahunui</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuamotu_archipelago" title="Tuamotu archipelago">Tuamotu archipelago</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beechey_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beechey-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li>1826 – <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gordon_Laing" title="Alexander Gordon Laing">Alexander Gordon Laing</a> becomes the first European to reach the fabled city of <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li>1827 – <a href="/wiki/Jedediah_Smith" title="Jedediah Smith">Jedediah Smith</a> crosses the Sierra Nevada (via <a href="/wiki/Ebbetts_Pass" title="Ebbetts Pass">Ebbetts Pass</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-14"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1828 – <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Cailli%C3%A9" title="René Caillié">René Caillié</a> is the first European to return alive from Timbuktu.</li>
<li>1829–30 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Ross_(Arctic_explorer)" title="John Ross (Arctic explorer)">John Ross</a> discovers "Boothia Felix" (the <a href="/wiki/Boothia_Peninsula" title="Boothia Peninsula">Boothia Peninsula</a>); the following year his nephew <a href="/wiki/James_Clark_Ross" title="James Clark Ross">James Clark Ross</a> crosses its narrow <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">isthmus</a> and reaches <a href="/wiki/King_William_Island" title="King William Island">King William Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edinger_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edinger-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li>1830 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Lemon_Lander" title="Richard Lemon Lander">Richard Lander</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/John_Lander_(explorer)" title="John Lander (explorer)">John</a> descend the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a> for more than 643 kilometres (400 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Bussa,_Nigeria" title="Bussa, Nigeria">Bussa</a> to its mouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2004_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2004-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>1831–32 – <a href="/wiki/John_Biscoe" title="John Biscoe">John Biscoe</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Enderby_Land" title="Enderby Land">Enderby Land</a>; following year discovers <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Island" title="Adelaide Island">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anvers_Island" title="Anvers Island">Anvers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biscoe_Islands" title="Biscoe Islands">Biscoe Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-5"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1833 – <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Glazunov" title="Andrei Glazunov">Andrei Glazunov</a> and Semyon Lukin discover the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Yukon_River" title="Yukon River">Yukon River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-15"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1833–35 – <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Pakhtusov" title="Pyotr Pakhtusov">Pyotr Pakhtusov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avgust_Tsivolko" title="Avgust Tsivolko">Avgust Tsivolko</a> chart the entire east coast of <a href="/wiki/Yuzhny_Island" title="Yuzhny Island">Yuzhny Island</a>, as well as the east coast of <a href="/wiki/Severny_Island" title="Severny Island">Severny Island</a> north to nearly 74°24’ N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-6"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1834 – <a href="/wiki/George_Back" title="George Back">George Back</a> descends the <a href="/wiki/Back_River_(Nunavut)" title="Back River (Nunavut)">Back River</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chantrey_Inlet" title="Chantrey Inlet">Chantrey Inlet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Back_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Back-104">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li>1837 – Glazunov ascends the <a href="/wiki/Unalakleet_River" title="Unalakleet River">Unalakleet</a> and portages to the middle Yukon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstoce_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstoce-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>1837–39 – <a href="/wiki/Peter_Warren_Dease" title="Peter Warren Dease">Peter Warren Dease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Simpson_(explorer)" title="Thomas Simpson (explorer)">Thomas Simpson</a> reach <a href="/wiki/Point_Barrow" title="Point Barrow">Point Barrow</a> from the east; following two summers they map the region from Point Turnagain to just north of the <a href="/wiki/Castor_and_Pollux_River" title="Castor and Pollux River">Castor and Pollux River</a> on the Boothia Peninsula and chart the coastline of "Victoria Land" (Victoria Island) from Point Back to Point Parry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-106">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li>1838 – Pyotr Malakhov reaches <a href="/wiki/Nulato,_Alaska" title="Nulato, Alaska">Nulato</a>, near the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Koyukuk_River" title="Koyukuk River">Koyukuk</a> and Yukon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstoce_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstoce-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>1838–40 – <a href="/wiki/Jules_Dumont_d%27Urville" title="Jules Dumont d'Urville">Jules Dumont d'Urville</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Joinville_Island_group" title="Joinville Island group">Joinville Island group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ad%C3%A9lie_Land" title="Adélie Land">Adélie Land</a> (138°21′ E).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-7"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1839 – <a href="/wiki/John_Balleny" title="John Balleny">John Balleny</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Balleny_Islands" title="Balleny Islands">Balleny Islands</a> and sights the <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_Coast" title="Sabrina Coast">Sabrina Coast</a> (121° E).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mawar_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mawar-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>1840 – <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wilkes" title="Charles Wilkes">Charles Wilkes</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Wilkes_Land" title="Wilkes Land">Wilkes Land</a>, mapping 2,414 kilometres (1,500 mi) of the Antarctic coast from Piner Bay (140° E) to the <a href="/wiki/Shackleton_Ice_Shelf" title="Shackleton Ice Shelf">Shackleton Ice Shelf</a> (97° E), proving that <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philbrick_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Philbrick-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li>1841–43 – James Clark Ross discovers the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Sea" title="Ross Sea">Ross Sea</a>, reaches 78°09′30″ S, and discovers the active volcano <a href="/wiki/Mount_Erebus" title="Mount Erebus">Mount Erebus</a> on <a href="/wiki/Ross_Island" title="Ross Island">Ross Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Ice_Shelf" title="Ross Ice Shelf">Ross Ice Shelf</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Land" title="Victoria Land">Victoria Land</a>; also sights <a href="/wiki/Snow_Hill_Island" title="Snow Hill Island">Snow Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Island" title="Seymour Island">Seymour</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Ross_Island" title="James Ross Island">James Ross Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross1843_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ross1843-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li>1845 – <a href="/wiki/John_Bell_(explorer)" title="John Bell (explorer)">John Bell</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Porcupine_River" title="Porcupine River">Porcupine</a>, which he descends to its confluence with the Yukon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstoce_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstoce-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>1846 – Candido José da Costa Cardoso discovers <a href="/wiki/Lake_Malawi" title="Lake Malawi">Lake Malawi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1846 – Rodrigues Graça travels from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)">Angola</a> to southwestern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Plateau" title="Katanga Plateau">Katanga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1846–47 – <a href="/wiki/John_Rae_(explorer)" title="John Rae (explorer)">John Rae</a> maps over 1,046 kilometres (650 mi) of coastline, from <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_Bay" title="Lord Mayor Bay">Lord Mayor Bay</a> to Cape Crozier, discovering <a href="/wiki/Committee_Bay" title="Committee Bay">Committee Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGoogan_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-McGoogan-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>c. 1847–48 – <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_da_Silva_Porto" title="António da Silva Porto">António da Silva Porto</a> reaches the upper <a href="/wiki/Zambezi" title="Zambezi">Zambezi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1848 – <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Rebmann" title="Johannes Rebmann">Johannes Rebmann</a> is the first to sight <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krapf_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krapf-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>1849 – <a href="/wiki/David_Livingstone" title="David Livingstone">David Livingstone</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Cotton_Oswell" title="William Cotton Oswell">William Cotton Oswell</a> cross the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a> to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ngami" title="Lake Ngami">Lake Ngami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1849 – James Clark Ross charts 240 kilometres (150 mi) of the west coast of Somerset Island south to Cape Coulman, discovering <a href="/wiki/Peel_Sound" title="Peel Sound">Peel Sound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>1850 – <a href="/wiki/Edwin_De_Haven" title="Edwin De Haven">Edwin De Haven</a> sails up <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Channel" title="Wellington Channel">Wellington Channel</a>, discovering and naming "Grinnell Land" (the <a href="/wiki/Grinnell_Peninsula" title="Grinnell Peninsula">Grinnell Peninsula</a>, which forms the northwestern corner of Devon Island).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>1850–54 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_McClure" title="Robert McClure">Robert McClure</a> transits the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">Northwest Passage</a> (by boat and sledge); he and his men also chart some 2,736 kilometres (1,700 mi) of new coastline, consisting of the entire coast of Banks Island and much of the northwestern coast of Victoria Island (from just east of Point Reynolds in the north to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Albert_Sound" title="Prince Albert Sound">Prince Albert Sound</a> in the south), in the process discovering <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Strait" title="Prince of Wales Strait">Prince of Wales Strait</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McClure_Strait" title="McClure Strait">McClure Strait</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Armstrong1_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Armstrong1-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li>1851 – Rae charts over 965 kilometres (600 mi) of the southern coastline of Victoria Island, from Cape Back to Pelly Point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGoogan_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-McGoogan-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>1851 – <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Ommanney" title="Erasmus Ommanney">Erasmus Ommanney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherard_Osborn" title="Sherard Osborn">Sherard Osborn</a> and William Browne chart the northern half of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Island_(Nunavut)" title="Prince of Wales Island (Nunavut)">Prince of Wales Island</a>, Osborn west to Sherard Osborn Point (72°20’ N) and Browne east to <a href="/wiki/Pandora_Island" title="Pandora Island">Pandora Island</a>; meanwhile, Robert D. Aldrich charts the west coast of the Bathurst Island group north to Cape Aldrich (about 76°11’ N, on <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Vanier" title="Île Vanier">Île Vanier</a>) and Dr. Abraham Bradford charts the east coast of Melville Island north to Bradford Point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-8"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Osborn1852_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Osborn1852-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>1851 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Campbell_(fur_trader)" title="Robert Campbell (fur trader)">Robert Campbell</a> descends the <a href="/wiki/Pelly_River" title="Pelly River">Pelly</a> to the Yukon, which he descends to its confluence with the Porcupine, reaching <a href="/wiki/Fort_Yukon,_Alaska" title="Fort Yukon, Alaska">Fort Yukon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstoce_105-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstoce-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>1851–52 – <a href="/wiki/William_Kennedy_(explorer)" title="William Kennedy (explorer)">William Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Ren%C3%A9_Bellot" title="Joseph René Bellot">Joseph René Bellot</a> discover <a href="/wiki/Bellot_Strait" title="Bellot Strait">Bellot Strait</a> and cross Prince of Wales Island east to west, reaching <a href="/wiki/Ommanney_Bay" title="Ommanney Bay">Ommanney Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>1852 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Augustus_Inglefield" title="Edward Augustus Inglefield">Edward Augustus Inglefield</a> reaches 78° 28’ N, entering Smith Sound; also charts Jones Sound as far west as 84° 10’ W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inglefield_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inglefield-115">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li>1852–53 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Belcher" title="Edward Belcher">Edward Belcher</a> sails two of his squadron to the northwestern coast of the Grinnell Peninsula, wintering at 77° 52’ N, 97° W; later circumnavigates the peninsula via Arthur Strait (now Fiord), discovering <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Island_(Nunavut)" title="Cornwall Island (Nunavut)">Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Kent_Island" title="North Kent Island">North Kent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-3"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>1853 – <a href="/wiki/Richard_Vesey_Hamilton" title="Richard Vesey Hamilton">Richard Vesey Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Henry_Richards" title="George Henry Richards">George Henry Richards</a> chart the Sabine Peninsula of Melville Island from Cape Mudge east to Bradford Point; the latter, along with Sherard Osborn, also charts the northern coast of Bathurst Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-4"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDougall_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-MDougall-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>1853 – <a href="/wiki/George_Mecham" title="George Mecham">George Mecham</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Prince_Patrick_Island" title="Prince Patrick Island">Prince Patrick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eglinton_Island" title="Eglinton Island">Eglinton Islands</a> and charts the southwest corner of Melville Island; along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_Leopold_McClintock" title="Francis Leopold McClintock">Francis Leopold McClintock</a>, he charts nearly the entire coast of Prince Patrick; McClintock also charts the northwest coast of Melville Island, from Cape Fisher northwest to Cape Scott and south along its west coast to Cape Purchase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDougall_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-MDougall-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>1853–54 – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elisha_Kent_Kane" title="Elisha Kent Kane">Elisha Kent Kane</a> and his men chart the <a href="/wiki/Kane_Basin" title="Kane Basin">Kane Basin</a> and discover <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Channel" title="Kennedy Channel">Kennedy Channel</a>; one of his men, William Morton, reaches as far north as Kap Constitution (81° 22’ N).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kane_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kane-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
