<li>1853–56 – Livingstone becomes the first to traverse Africa from west to east, traveling from <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> in Angola to <a href="/wiki/Quelimane" title="Quelimane">Quelimane</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>; also explores much of the upper Zambezi and discovers and names <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Falls,_Zambia" title="Victoria Falls, Zambia">Victoria Falls</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal1973_88-5"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal1973-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>1854 – Rae charts the Boothia Peninsula from the Castor and Pollux River north to Point de la Guiche, discovering <a href="/wiki/Rae_Strait" title="Rae Strait">Rae Strait</a> and proving the insularity of King William Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGoogan_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-McGoogan-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>1858 – <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis_Burton" title="Richard Francis Burton">Richard Francis Burton</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Hanning_Speke" title="John Hanning Speke">John Hanning Speke</a> discover <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Speke_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Speke-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li>1859 – McClintock charts the remaining 193 kilometres (120 mi) of the continental coastline of America (on the west coast of the Boothia Peninsula), while his companion <a href="/wiki/Allen_Young" title="Allen Young">Allen Young</a> charts the southern half of Prince of Wales Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savours_111-5"><a href="#cite_note-Savours-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>1860–61 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_O%27Hara_Burke" title="Robert O'Hara Burke">Robert O'Hara Burke</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_John_Wills" title="William John Wills">William Wills</a> are the first to cross Australia from south to north, traveling from <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Flinders_River" title="Flinders River">Flinders River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2004_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2004-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>1862 – Speke discovers the Nile flowing from the northern end of Lake Victoria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2004_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2004-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>1862 – Ivan Lukin ascends the Yukon to Fort Yukon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstoce_105-4"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstoce-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>1864 – <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Baker" title="Samuel Baker">Samuel Baker</a> discovers "Luta Nzige" (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Albert_(Africa)" title="Lake Albert (Africa)">Lake Albert</a>); in the distance he sights the <a href="/wiki/Mountains_of_the_Moon_(Africa)" title="Mountains of the Moon (Africa)">Mountains of the Moon</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Rwenzori_Mountains" title="Rwenzori Mountains">Rwenzori</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2004_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2004-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>1865 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Whymper" title="Edward Whymper">Edward Whymper</a> is the first to ascend the <a href="/wiki/Matterhorn" title="Matterhorn">Matterhorn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2004_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2004-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>1869–70 – <a href="/wiki/Carl_Koldewey" title="Carl Koldewey">Carl Koldewey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julius_von_Payer" title="Julius von Payer">Julius von Payer</a> explore the east coast of Greenland from 74°18’ to 77°01’N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1871 – <a href="/wiki/Charles_Francis_Hall" title="Charles Francis Hall">Charles Francis Hall</a> reaches <a href="/wiki/Robeson_Channel" title="Robeson Channel">Robeson Channel</a>, sailing his ship as far north as 82° 11’ N; he later travels by sledge to 83° 05’ N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dick_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dick-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>1872 – William Adams proves the insularity of Bylot Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-9"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1873–74 – <a href="/wiki/Karl_Weyprecht" title="Karl Weyprecht">Karl Weyprecht</a> and Von Payer discover and name <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1875–76 – <a href="/wiki/George_Nares" title="George Nares">George Nares</a> sails as far north as 82° 24’ N; following year <a href="/wiki/Albert_Hastings_Markham" title="Albert Hastings Markham">Albert Hastings Markham</a> sledges to 83° 20’ 26" N, while <a href="/wiki/Pelham_Aldrich" title="Pelham Aldrich">Pelham Aldrich</a> sledges along the northern coast of Ellesmere Island east to Alert Point and <b>Lewis A. Beaumont</b> explores the northwestern coast of Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dick_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dick-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>1875–77 – <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morton_Stanley" title="Henry Morton Stanley">Henry Morton Stanley</a> circumnavigates both Lakes Tanganyika and Victoria, sights <a href="/wiki/Lake_George_(Uganda)" title="Lake George (Uganda)">Lake George</a>, and descends the <a href="/wiki/Lualaba_River" title="Lualaba River">Lualaba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo</a> to the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>1876 – <a href="/wiki/Luigi_D%27Albertis" title="Luigi D'Albertis">Luigi D'Albertis</a> ascends over 800 kilometres (500 mi) up the <a href="/wiki/Fly_River" title="Fly River">Fly River</a> in New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Albertis_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Albertis-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li>1878–79 – <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Erik_Nordenski%C3%B6ld" title="Adolf Erik Nordenskiöld">Adolf Erik Nordenskiöld</a> is the first to transit the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northeast Passage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leslie1879_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leslie1879-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li>1881–83 – <a href="/wiki/Adolphus_Greely" title="Adolphus Greely">Adolphus Greely</a> explores the interior of Ellesmere Island, discovering <a href="/wiki/Lake_Hazen" title="Lake Hazen">Lake Hazen</a>; one of his men, <a href="/wiki/James_Booth_Lockwood" title="James Booth Lockwood">James Booth Lockwood</a>, crosses the island and reaches <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greely_Fiord" title="Greely Fiord">Greely Fiord</a>, as well as sledging eastwards to the vicinity of Kap Washington (reaching 83° 23’08" N in the process).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dick_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dick-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>1883–84 – <a href="/wiki/Franz_Boas" title="Franz Boas">Franz Boas</a> is the first to see <a href="/wiki/Nettilling_Lake" title="Nettilling Lake">Nettilling Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-10"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1887–89 – Stanley traverses the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_Rainforest" title="Ituri Rainforest">Ituri Rainforest</a>, explores the Rwenzori, and follows the <a href="/wiki/Semliki_River" title="Semliki River">Semliki</a> to its source (which he names <a href="/wiki/Lake_Edward" title="Lake Edward">Lake Edward</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jeal_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jeal-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>1892 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peary" title="Robert Peary">Robert Peary</a> discovers and names <a href="/wiki/Independence_Fjord" title="Independence Fjord">Independence Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peary_Land" title="Peary Land">Peary Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1893–96 – <a href="/wiki/Fridtjof_Nansen" title="Fridtjof Nansen">Fridtjof Nansen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_Johansen" title="Hjalmar Johansen">Hjalmar Johansen</a> sledge to 86°13'06" N; their ship, the <a href="/wiki/Fram" title="Fram">Fram</a>, under <a href="/wiki/Otto_Sverdrup" title="Otto Sverdrup">Otto Sverdrup</a>, drifts in the ice from the New Siberian Islands west to the northwest coast of Spitsbergen, reaching 85°55'05" N—a new record for a ship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1898–1902 – Sverdrup and <a href="/wiki/Gunnar_Isachsen" title="Gunnar Isachsen">Gunnar Isachsen</a> chart the western coast of Ellesmere Island and discover and name <a href="/wiki/Axel_Heiberg_Island" title="Axel Heiberg Island">Axel Heiberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ellef_Ringnes_Island" title="Ellef Ringnes Island">Ellef Ringnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amund_Ringnes_Island" title="Amund Ringnes Island">Amund Ringnes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/King_Christian_Island" title="King Christian Island">King Christian Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sverdrup_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sverdrup-125">[125]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_European_exploration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="321" data-file-width="486" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg/220px-Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg/330px-Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg/440px-Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amundsen's party at the South Pole, December 1911. From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Roald_Amundsen" title="Roald Amundsen">Amundsen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmer_Hanssen" title="Helmer Hanssen">Hanssen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sverre_Hassel" title="Sverre Hassel">Hassel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wisting" title="Oscar Wisting">Wisting</a> (photo by fifth member <a href="/wiki/Olav_Bjaaland" title="Olav Bjaaland">Bjaaland)</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scottgroup.jpg"><img alt="Five men in heavy clothing and headgear; three are standing and two seated on the ground. The standing men carry flags; all five have dejected expressions" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2400" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Scottgroup.jpg/220px-Scottgroup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Scottgroup.jpg/330px-Scottgroup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Scottgroup.jpg/440px-Scottgroup.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scottgroup.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scott's party at the South Pole, 18 January 1912. L to R: (standing) <a href="/wiki/Edward_Adrian_Wilson" title="Edward Adrian Wilson">Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falcon_Scott" title="Robert Falcon Scott">Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Oates" title="Lawrence Oates">Oates</a>; (seated) <a href="/wiki/Henry_Robertson_Bowers" title="Henry Robertson Bowers">Bowers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Evans" title="Edgar Evans">Edgar Evans</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg/220px-Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg/330px-Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg/440px-Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Severnaya_Zemlya_-_raising_of_the_Russian_flag_in_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Severnaya Zemlya – raising of the Russian flag in 1913.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>1900 – Peary explores the north coast of Greenland from Kap Washington to Kap Clarence Wyckoff, on the way reaching <a href="/wiki/Cape_Morris_Jesup" title="Cape Morris Jesup">Cape Morris Jesup</a>, the most northern point of mainland Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mirsky_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mirsky-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li>1902–04 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falcon_Scott" title="Robert Falcon Scott">Robert Falcon Scott</a> traces the length of the Ross Ice Shelf, discovers the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_Peninsula" title="Edward VII Peninsula">Edward VII Peninsula</a>, reaches about 82°11’ S (in the process tracing 600 kilometres (370 mi) of the west coast of the shelf), crosses the <a href="/wiki/Transantarctic_Mountains" title="Transantarctic Mountains">Transantarctic Mountains</a> and discovers the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Plateau" title="Antarctic Plateau">Antarctic Plateau</a>, penetrating nearly 240 kilometres (150 mi) into it; he is also the first to see the <a href="/wiki/McMurdo_Dry_Valleys" title="McMurdo Dry Valleys">dry valleys</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crane_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crane-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li>1903–06 – <a href="/wiki/Roald_Amundsen" title="Roald Amundsen">Roald Amundsen</a> transits the Northwest Passage in the sloop <i><a href="/wiki/Gj%C3%B8a" title="Gjøa">Gjøa</a></i>; Godfred Hansen, his second-in-command, charts the east coast of Victoria Island north to Cape Nansen (72°02' N, 104°45' W).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amundsen_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amundsen-128">[128]</a></sup></li>
<li>1906–07 – <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_Mylius-Erichsen" title="Ludvig Mylius-Erichsen">Ludvig Mylius-Erichsen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johan_Peter_Koch" title="Johan Peter Koch">Johan Peter Koch</a> chart the northeast coast of Greenland from Kap Bismarck (76°42' N) to Kap Clarence Wyckoff (82°52' N), discovering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danmark_Fjord" title="Danmark Fjord">Danmark Fjord</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-11"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1908–09 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Cook" title="Frederick Cook">Frederick Cook</a> and Peary each claim to have reached the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>—the former is a fraud, the latter widely doubted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1910–11 – <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Hantzsch" title="Bernhard Hantzsch">Bernhard Hantzsch</a> crosses Baffin Island from Cumberland Sound to the <a href="/wiki/Koukdjuak_River" title="Koukdjuak River">Koukdjuak River</a>, exploring the west coast of the island north to 68°45’N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-12"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1911–12 – Amundsen is the first to reach the <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a>; Scott and his team reach the Pole over a month later, all perishing on the return journey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crane_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crane-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li>1913–14 – <a href="/wiki/Boris_Vilkitsky" title="Boris Vilkitsky">Boris Vilkitsky</a> and Per Novopashennyy discover <a href="/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya" title="Severnaya Zemlya">Severnaya Zemlya</a>, surveying parts of its eastern coast from <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Cape" title="Arctic Cape">Mys Arkticheskiy</a> to Mys Vaygacha (its southeast point), as well as much of its south coast west to Mys Neupokoyeva.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr1975_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barr1975-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>1915–17 – <a href="/wiki/Vilhjalmur_Stefansson" title="Vilhjalmur Stefansson">Vilhjalmur Stefansson</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Brock_Island" title="Brock Island">Brock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_King_Island" title="Mackenzie King Island">Mackenzie King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borden_Island" title="Borden Island">Borden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meighen_Island" title="Meighen Island">Meighen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lougheed_Island" title="Lougheed Island">Lougheed Islands</a>; one of his men, Storker T. Storkerson, charts part of the northeast coast of Victoria Island, discovering the Storkerson Peninsula and <a href="/wiki/Stefansson_Island" title="Stefansson Island">Stefansson Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-13"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stefansson_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stefansson-130">[130]</a></sup></li>
<li>1924–29 – <a href="/wiki/J._Dewey_Soper" title="J. Dewey Soper">Joseph Dewey Soper</a> explores the interior of Baffin Island before surveying its west coast north to Hantzsch River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-14"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1926 – Amundsen, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Ellsworth" title="Lincoln Ellsworth">Lincoln Ellsworth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Nobile" title="Umberto Nobile">Umberto Nobile</a> in the airship <a href="/wiki/Norge_(airship)" title="Norge (airship)">Norge</a> are the first definitely known to have sighted the North Pole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2001_120-5"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2001-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>1927 – <a href="/wiki/George_P._Putnam" title="George P. Putnam">George P. Putnam</a> charts the north coast of the Foxe Peninsula from Cape Dorchester to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bowman_Bay,_Nunavut" title="Bowman Bay, Nunavut">Bowman Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-15"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1930–32 – <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Ushakov" title="Georgy Ushakov">Georgy Ushakov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Urvantsev" title="Nikolay Urvantsev">Nikolay Urvantsev</a> survey the entire coast of Severnaya Zemlya, showing it to be made up of four main islands: <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution_Island" title="October Revolution Island">October Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Komsomolets_Island" title="Komsomolets Island">Komsomolets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Island_(Russia)" title="Pioneer Island (Russia)">Pioneer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Island" title="Bolshevik Island">Bolshevik Islands</a>—in all surveying some 2,200 kilometres (1,400 mi) of coastline and interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr1975_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barr1975-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>1932 – W. A. Poole discovers <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles_Island" title="Prince Charles Island">Prince Charles Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>1934 – <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Byrd" title="Richard E. Byrd">Richard E. Byrd</a> discovers and names <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island,_Antarctica" title="Roosevelt Island, Antarctica">Roosevelt Island</a>.</li>
<li>1937–41 – <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Henry_Manning" title="Thomas Henry Manning">Thomas and Ella Manning</a> map the west coast of Baffin Island from the Hantzsch River to <a href="/wiki/Steensby_Inlet" title="Steensby Inlet">Steensby Inlet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_77-16"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1940 – Byrd discovers <a href="/wiki/Thurston_Island" title="Thurston Island">Thurston Island</a>, believing it to be a peninsula.</li>
<li>1948 – E. C. Kerslake charts Prince Charles, <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Island" title="Air Force Island">Air Force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foley_Island" title="Foley Island">Foley Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_29-16"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>1950 – <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Herzog" title="Maurice Herzog">Maurice Herzog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Lachenal" title="Louis Lachenal">Louis Lachenal</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1950_French_Annapurna_expedition" title="1950 French Annapurna expedition">French Annapurna expedition</a> become the first climbers to reach the summit of an <a href="/wiki/Eight-thousander" title="Eight-thousander">8,000-metre</a> peak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herzog1997_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herzog1997-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>1953 – <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Hillary" title="Edmund Hillary">Edmund Hillary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenzing_Norgay" title="Tenzing Norgay">Tenzing Norgay</a> are the first to ascend <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HighAdventure_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-HighAdventure-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>1954 – <a href="/wiki/Lino_Lacedelli" title="Lino Lacedelli">Lino Lacedelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Achille_Compagnoni" title="Achille Compagnoni">Achille Compagnoni</a> are the first to ascend <a href="/wiki/K2" title="K2">K2</a> on the <a href="/wiki/1954_Italian_Karakoram_expedition_to_K2" title="1954 Italian Karakoram expedition to K2">Italian Karakoram expedition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>1957 – <a href="/wiki/Finn_Ronne" title="Finn Ronne">Finn Ronne</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Berkner_Island" title="Berkner Island">Berkner Island</a>.</li></ul>
